<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Illegal immigration</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_emigration" title="Illegal emigration">Illegal emigration</a></div>
<p><b>Illegal immigration</b> is the migration of people across national <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">borders</a> in a way that violates the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_law" title="Immigration law">immigration laws</a> of the destination country. Immigration, including illegal immigration, is overwhelmingly upward, from a poorer to a richer country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> However, it is also noted that illegal immigrants tend not to be the poorest within the populations they emigrate from. Some countries have millions of illegal immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>When potential immigrants believe that the chances/benefits of successfully migrating are greater than the risks/costs, illegal immigration becomes an option. The benefits taken into account include not only expected improvements in income and living conditions, but also expectations in relation to potential future residential permits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> where illegal immigrants are given a path to <a href="/wiki/Naturalization" title="Naturalization">naturalization</a> or <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feere_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-feere-4">[4]</a></sup> The costs may include restrictions on living as an illegal immigrant in the destination country, leaving family and ways of life behind, the experience of visible or verbal disdain by native-born residents in the host country, and the probability of being detained and resulting sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There have been campaigns to discourage the use of the term "illegal immigrant" in many countries since 2007, generally based on the argument that the act of immigration may be illegal in some cases, but the people themselves are not illegal. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, a "Drop the I-Word" campaign was launched in 2010 to advocate the use of terms such as "<b>undocumented immigrants</b>" or "<b>unauthorized immigrants</b>" to refer to the foreign nationals who reside in a country illegally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The term "<b>illegalized immigrant</b>" is being advocated by some, arguing that it draws attention away from the individual immigrants and focus on the state, as the state makes it illegal for some foreign nationals to reside in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>News associations that have discontinued or discourage the use of the adjective "illegal" to describe people include the US <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> UK <a href="/wiki/Press_Association" title="Press Association">Press Association</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Journalism_Observatory" title="European Journalism Observatory">European Journalism Observatory</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Journalism_Centre" title="European Journalism Centre">European Journalism Centre</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_of_European_Journalists" title="Association of European Journalists">Association of European Journalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Press_Council" title="Australian Press Council">Australian Press Council</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and Australian <a href="/wiki/Media,_Entertainment_and_Arts_Alliance" title="Media, Entertainment and Arts Alliance">Media, Entertainment and Arts Alliance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Related terms that do not describe people directly are not necessarily affected by this argument. For example, Associated Press still uses the term "illegal immigration" to describe the action of entering or residing in a country illegally.</p>
<p>In contrast, in some contexts the term "illegal immigrants" is shortened to "<b>illegals</b>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_models_of_illegal_immigration">Economic models of illegal immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Economic models of illegal immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_migration#Theories_for_migration_for_work_in_the_21st_century" title="Human migration">Human_migration § Theories for migration for work in the 21st century</a></div>
<p>There are multiple models that explain illegal immigration from the perspective of the potential immigrants.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neoclassical_model">Neoclassical model</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Neoclassical model">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Neoclassical theory posits that fact employment, and chances of future legal status govern the likelihood of "successful" illegal immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-logic_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-logic-17">[17]</a></sup> This model also assumes that illegal workers tend to add to, and compete with, the receiving countries' pool of unskilled laborers. Illegal workers in this model find employment by accepting lower wages than native-born workers, sometimes below the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> and "off-the-books." Economist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Borjas" title="George Borjas">George Borjas</a> supports aspects of this model, calculating that real wages of US workers without a high school degree declined by 9% from 1980–2000 due to competition from illegal immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Large-scale economic evidence supports neoclassical theory, as may be seen in the long-term correlation of relative wages and unemployment with illegal immigration from Mexico to the US. However, migration scholars such as <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Hanson" title="Gordon Hanson">Gordon Hanson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Massey" title="Douglas Massey">Douglas Massey</a> have criticized the model for being oversimplified and not accounting for contradictory evidence, such as low net illegal immigration from Mexico to the US before the 1980s despite significant economic disparity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-logic_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-logic-17">[17]</a></sup> Numerous refinements have been suggested to account for other factors, as seen below.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_liberalization">Trade liberalization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Trade liberalization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In recent years, developing states have pursued the benefits of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> by adopting measures to liberalize trade. But rapid opening of domestic markets may lead to displacement of large numbers of agricultural or unskilled workers, who are more likely to seek employment and a higher quality of life by illegal immigration. This is a frequently cited argument to explain how the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> may have impoverished Mexican farmers who were unable to compete with the higher productivity of US subsidized agriculture, especially for corn. NAFTA may have also unexpectedly raised educational requirements for industrial jobs in Mexico, since the new <i><a href="/wiki/Maquiladora" title="Maquiladora">maquiladoras</a></i> produced export products requiring skills and education that many unskilled workers did not have.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pietro_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-pietro-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_demand_in_developed_states">Structural demand in developed states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Structural demand in developed states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Douglas_Massey" title="Douglas Massey">Douglas Massey</a> argues that a bifurcating labor market in so called developed countries creates a <b>structural demand</b> for unskilled immigrant labor to fill undesirable jobs which native-born citizens do not seek, regardless of wages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massey_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-massey-20">[20]</a></sup> He postulates that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postindustrial" title="Postindustrial">postindustrial</a> economies have a widening gap between well-paying, white-collar jobs that require ever higher levels of education ("human capital"), for which native-born citizens and legal immigrants can qualify, and bottom-tier jobs that are <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">stigmatized</a> and require no education. These "underclass" jobs include harvesting crops, unskilled labor in landscaping and construction, house-cleaning, and maid and busboy work in hotels and restaurants, all of which have a disproportionate number of illegal immigrants. Research indicates that the advantage to firms from employing illegal immigrants increases as more firms in the industry do so, decreases with the skill level of the firm's workers, increases with the breadth of a firm's market, and increases with the labor intensity of the firm's production process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the decline of middle-class <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue-collar" title="Blue-collar">blue-collar</a> jobs in manufacturing and industry, younger native-born generations have acquired higher education. The majority of new blue-collar jobs qualify as Massey's "underclass" work, and suffer from unreliability, subservient roles and, critically, a lack of potential for advancement. Entry-level white-collar and service jobs offer advancement opportunities for people with work permits and citizenship.</p>
<p>In a developed country like the US, only 12% of the labor force has less than a high school education. Illegal immigrants are believed to have lower levels of education, and it has been reported that about 70% of illegal workers in the US from Mexico lack a high school degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-logic_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-logic-17">[17]</a></sup> Even "underclass" jobs have higher relative wages than those in home countries. Since many illegal immigrants often anticipate working only temporarily in the destination country, the lack of opportunity for advancement is seen by many as less of a problem. Some support for this claim can be seen in a Pew Hispanic Center poll of over 3,000 illegal immigrants from Mexico in the US, which found that 79% would voluntarily join a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temporary_worker" title="Temporary worker">temporary worker</a> program that allowed them to work legally for several years but then required them to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_survey_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew_survey-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The structural demand theory posits that willingness to take undesirable jobs is what gives illegal immigrants their employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massey_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-massey-20">[20]</a></sup> Evidence for this may be seen in the average wages of illegal day laborers in California, between $10 and $12 per hour in a 2005 study, was higher than many entry-level white collar work or service jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Structural demand theory argues that cases like this show that there is no direct competition between illegal immigrants and native-born workers. This is the concept that illegal immigrants "take jobs that no one else wants." Massey argues that this has certain policy implications, as it may refute claims that illegal immigrants are "lowering wages" or stealing jobs from native-born workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massey_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-massey-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty">Poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>While economic models do look at relative wealth and income between home and destination countries, they do not necessarily imply that illegal immigrants are always impoverished by standards of the home country. The poorest classes in a developing country may lack the resources needed to mount an attempt to cross illegally, or the connections to friends or family already in the destination country. Studies from the Pew Hispanic Center have shown that the education and wage levels of illegal Mexican immigrants in the US are around the median for Mexico, and that having family who have immigrated or being from a community with many immigrants is a much better predictor of one's choice to immigrate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_survey_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-pew_survey-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other examples do show that increases in poverty, especially when associated with immediate crises, can increase the likelihood of illegal migration. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_economic_crisis_in_Mexico" title="1994 economic crisis in Mexico">1994 economic crisis in Mexico</a>, subsequent to the start of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA), was associated with widespread poverty and a lower valuation for the peso relative to the dollar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pietro_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-pietro-19">[19]</a></sup> It also marked the start of a massive swell in Mexican immigration, in which net illegal migration to the US increased every year from the mid-1990s until the mid-2000s.</p>
<p>There are also examples where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_disasters" title="Natural disasters">natural disasters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">overpopulation</a> can amplify <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>-driven migration flows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overpopulation">Overpopulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Overpopulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">Population growth</a> that exceeds the <a href="/wiki/Carrying_capacity" title="Carrying capacity">carrying capacity</a> of an area or environment results in <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">overpopulation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Spikes in human population can cause problems such as <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_crisis" title="Water crisis">water crisis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">World population</a> has grown from 1.6 billion in 1900 to an estimated <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Seven_Billion" title="Day of Seven Billion">7 billion in 2011</a>. In Mexico alone, population has grown from 13.6 million in 1900 to 107 million in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Virginia Abernethy notes that immigration is a road that provides a "relief valve" to overpopulation that stops a population from addressing the consequences of its overpopulation and that exports this overpopulation to another location or country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimated that the world's population was growing at the rate of 1.14% (or about 75 million people) per year. According to data from the CIA's <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">World Factbook</a>, the world human population currently increases by 145 every minute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Census_Bureau" title="Census Bureau">Census Bureau</a> issued a revised forecast for world population that increased its projection for the year 2050 to above 9.4 billion people, up from 9.1 billion people. There are a billion more added every 12 years. Almost all growth will take place in the less developed regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_reunification_in_new_country_of_residence">Family reunification in new country of residence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Family reunification in new country of residence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some illegal immigrants seek to live with loved ones, such as a spouse or other family members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washpost1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-washpost1-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lamigra_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-lamigra-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haaretz1_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-haaretz1-36">[36]</a></sup> Family reunification visas may be applied for by legal residents or naturalized citizens to bring their family members into a destination state legally, but these visas may be limited in number and subject to yearly quotas. This may force their family members to enter illegally to reunify. From studying Mexican migration patterns, Douglas Massey finds that the likelihood that a Mexican national will emigrate illegally to the US increases dramatically if they have one or more family members already residing in the United States, legally or illegally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massey_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-massey-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wars_and_asylum">Wars and asylum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Wars and asylum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4992" data-file-width="7581" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg/350px-20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg/525px-20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg/700px-20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20101009_Arrested_refugees_immigrants_in_Fylakio_detention_center_Thrace_Evros_Greece_restored.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arrested refugees-immigrants in Fylakio detention center, Evros, Greece.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Illegal immigration may be prompted by the desire to escape civil war or <a href="/wiki/Political_repression" title="Political repression">repression</a> in the country of origin. Non-economic push factors include <a href="/wiki/Persecution" title="Persecution">persecution</a> (religious and otherwise), frequent <a href="/wiki/Physical_abuse" title="Physical abuse">abuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">oppression</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, and risks to civilians during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_wars" title="List of wars">war</a>. Political motives traditionally motivate <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee</a> flows – to escape <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorship</a> for instance.</p>
<p>The status of "illegal immigrant" may coincide with or be replaced by the status of "<a href="/wiki/Asylum_seeker" title="Asylum seeker">asylum seeker</a>" for emigrants who have escaped a war or repression and have unlawfully crossed into another state. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asylum_seekers" title="Asylum seekers">Asylum seekers</a> are generally not considered to be illegal immigrants unless they remain in a country after they are determined not to have valid reasons to receive asylum. If they are recognized as "legitimate" asylees by the destination state, they will then gain status. However, there may be numerous potential asylums in a destination state who are unwilling to apply or have been denied asylum status, and hence are categorized as "illegal immigrants" and may be subject to punishment or deportation. However, Article 31 of the <a href="/wiki/Convention_Relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" title="Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees">Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees</a> prohibits the Contracting States from imposing penalties on refugees for their illegal enter or presence, who come directly from a territory where their life or freedom are threatened. There are numerous cases of mass emigration from poor or war-stricken states. These include examples from Africa,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Colombia, and El Salvador.</p>
<p>After decades of armed conflict, roughly one of every 10 Colombians now lives abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mis1_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-mis1-38">[38]</a></sup> For example, Colombians emigrating to Spain have "grown exponentially, from a little over 7,000 in 1993 to more than 80,000 in 2002 and 244,000 in 2003."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdiversity_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdiversity-39">[39]</a></sup> According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="U.S. Department of Homeland Security">U.S. Department of Homeland Security</a> indicate that <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> is the fourth-leading source country of illegal <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">immigration to the United States</a>. According to its <a href="/wiki/Estimates" title="Estimates">estimates</a>, the number of illegal Colombian residents in the United States almost tripled from 51,000 in 1990 to 141,000 in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ins_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ins-40">[40]</a></sup> According to the US Census Bureau, the number of people born in Colombia living in the United States in 2013 was about 680,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> is another country which experienced substantial emigration as a result of civil war and repression. The largest per-capita source of immigrants to the United States comes from El Salvador. In 2013, there were about 1.25 million people born in El Salvador living in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-41">[41]</a></sup> equal to about one-fifth the current population of El Salvador.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deprivation_of_citizenship">Deprivation of citizenship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Deprivation of citizenship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a 2012 news story, the <a href="/wiki/Common_Sense_Media" title="Common Sense Media"><i>CSM</i></a> reported, "The estimated 750,000 <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Rohingya</a>, one of the most miserable and oppressed minorities in the world, are deeply resentful of their almost complete absence of civil rights in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>. In 1982, the military junta stripped the Rohingya of their Myanmar citizenship, classing them as undocumented immigrants and rendering them <a href="/wiki/Statelessness" title="Statelessness">stateless</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denaturalization" title="Denaturalization">Denaturalization</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_faced_by_illegal_immigrants">Problems faced by illegal immigrants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Problems faced by illegal immigrants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Illegal immigrants may expose themselves and citizens of the countries they enter to dangers and diseases while entering another country. Aside from the possibility that they may be intercepted and deported, illegal immigrants may be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trafficking_in_human_beings" title="Trafficking in human beings">trafficked</a> for exploitation including <a href="/wiki/Sexual_slavery" title="Sexual slavery">sexual exploitation</a> and some illegal immigrants, are involved in criminal activity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery">Slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_Trafficking" title="Human Trafficking">Human Trafficking</a></div>
<p>After the end of the legal international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> by the Europeans and the United States in the early 19th century, the illegal importation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">slaves</a> has continued, albeit at much reduced levels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, research at <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_State_University" title="San Diego State University">San Diego State University</a> estimates that there are 2.4 million victims of human trafficking among illegal Mexican immigrants in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Although not as common as in Europe, Asia, Africa and Latin America<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, some women are smuggled into the United States and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>People have been kidnapped or tricked into slavery to work as laborers, after entering the country, for example in factories. Those trafficked in this manner often face additional barriers to escaping slavery, since their status as illegal immigrants makes it difficult for them to gain access to help or services. For example, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burmese</a> women trafficked into Thailand and forced to work in factories or as prostitutes may not speak the language and may be vulnerable to abuse by police due to their illegal immigrant status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In some regions, people that are still en route to their destination country are also sometimes kidnapped, for example for <a href="/wiki/Ransom" title="Ransom">ransom</a>. In some instances, they are also <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">tortured</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">raped</a>, and killed if the requested ransom does not arrive. One case in point are the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Eritrea" title="Demographics of Eritrea">Eritrean</a> migrants that are en route to Israel. A large number of them are captured in north Sinai (Egypt) and Eastern Sudan and held in the buildings in north Sinai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prostitution">Prostitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Prostitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sex_Trafficking" title="Sex Trafficking">Sex Trafficking</a></div>
<p>Some people forced into <a href="/wiki/Sexual_slavery" title="Sexual slavery">sexual slavery</a> face challenges of charges of illegal immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">fall of the Iron Curtain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> is being confronted with a serious problem related to the sexual exploitation of illegal immigrants (especially from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>), for the purpose of prostitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States human trafficking victims often pass through the porous Mexican border. In an effort to curb the spread of this affliction, California Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Kamala_Harris" title="Kamala Harris">Kamala Harris</a> and Mexico Attorney General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marisela_Morales_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez" title="Marisela Morales Ibáñez">Marisela Morales Ibáñez</a> signed an accord in 2012 to expand prosecutions of criminals typically members of transnational gangs who engage in the trafficking of human beings between the two countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Injury_and_Illness">Injury and Illness</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Injury and Illness">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The search for employment is central to undocumented international migration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> According to data from the U.S. Census Bureau, undocumented immigrants to the United States often work in dangerous industries such as agriculture and construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> A recent study suggests that the complex web of consequences resulting from undocumented status limits immigrant workers' ability to stay safe at work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In addition to physical danger at work, the choice to immigrate for work often entails work-induced lifestyle factors which impact the physical, mental and social health of immigrants and their families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Each year there are several hundred illegal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant_deaths_along_the_U.S.-Mexico_border" title="Immigrant deaths along the U.S.-Mexico border">Immigrant deaths along the U.S.-Mexico border</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Death by exposure occurs in the deserts of Southwestern United States during the hot summer season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">Methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_crossing">Border crossing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Border crossing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="800" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/220px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/330px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/440px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Border patrol at sea by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">U.S. Customs and Border Protection</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg/220px-HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg/330px-HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg/440px-HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMRC_Vigilant_BB.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
HMC Vigilant, one of several customs cutters of the UKBA, capable of speeds up to 26 knots departing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Naval_Base" title="Portsmouth Naval Base">Portsmouth Naval Base</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Immigrants from countries that do not have automatic visa agreements, or who would not otherwise qualify for a visa, often cross the borders illegally in some areas like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico_border" title="United States–Mexico border">United States–Mexico border</a>, the Mona Channel between the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Otranto" title="Strait of Otranto">Strait of Otranto</a>. Because these methods are illegal, they are often dangerous. Would-be immigrants have been known to suffocate in <a href="/wiki/Shipping_container" title="Shipping container">shipping containers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Boxcar" title="Boxcar">boxcars</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and trucks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> sink in <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecks</a> caused by unseaworthy vessels, die of <a href="/wiki/Dehydration" title="Dehydration">dehydration</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Hypothermia" title="Hypothermia">exposure</a> during long walks without water. An official estimate puts the number of people who died in illegal crossings across the U.S.-Mexican border between 1998 and 2004 at 1,954 (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant_deaths_along_the_U.S.-Mexico_border" title="Immigrant deaths along the U.S.-Mexico border">immigrant deaths along the U.S.-Mexico border</a>).</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_smuggling" title="Human smuggling">Human smuggling</a> is the practice of intermediaries aiding illegal immigrants in crossing over international borders in financial gain, often in large groups. Human smuggling differs from, but is sometimes associated with, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>. A human smuggler will facilitate <a href="/wiki/Illegal_entry" title="Illegal entry">illegal entry</a> into a country for a fee, but on arrival at their destination, the smuggled person is usually free. Trafficking involves a process of using physical force, <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Deception" title="Deception">deception</a> to obtain and transport people.</p>
<p>Types of notorious human smugglers include <a href="/wiki/Snakehead_(gang)" title="Snakehead (gang)">Snakehead</a> <a href="/wiki/Gang" title="Gang">gangs</a> present in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> (especially in <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>) that smuggle laborers into <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a> states (making <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> frequent centers of illegal immigration) and "coyotes", who smuggle illegal immigrants to the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a> and have been known to abuse or even kill their passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Sometimes illegal immigrants are abandoned by their human traffickers if there are difficulties, often dying in the process. Others may be victims of intentional killing.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overstaying_a_visa">Overstaying a visa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Overstaying a visa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many illegal immigrants are migrants who originally arrive in a country lawfully but overstay their authorized residence (overstaying a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" title="Visa (document)">visa</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iom5_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-iom5-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> For example, most of the estimated 200,000 illegal immigrants in Canada (perhaps as high as 500,000) are refugee claimants whose refugee applications were rejected but who have not yet been expelled from the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another example is formed by children of foreigners born in countries observing <i><a href="/wiki/Jus_soli" title="Jus soli">jus soli</a></i> ("right of territory"), such as was the case in France until 1994<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and in Ireland until 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizensinformation.ie_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-citizensinformation.ie-66">[66]</a></sup> In these countries, it was possible to obtain French or Irish nationality (respectively) solely by being born in France before 1994 or in Ireland before 2005<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizensinformation.ie_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-citizensinformation.ie-66">[66]</a></sup> (respectively). At present, a French born child of foreign parents does not automatically obtain French nationality until residency duration conditions are met<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Since 1 January 2005, a child born in Ireland does not automatically acquire Irish nationality unless certain conditions are met.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizensinformation.ie_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-citizensinformation.ie-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sham_marriages">Sham marriages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sham marriages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another method is by entering into a <a href="/wiki/Sham_marriage" title="Sham marriage">sham marriage</a> where the marriage is contracted into for purely immigration advantage by a couple who are not in a genuine relationship. Common reasons for sham marriages are to gain <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> residency, work or <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> rights for one or both of the spouses, or for other benefits.</p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, those who arrange, participate in, or officiate over a sham marriage may be charged with a number of offenses, including assisting unlawful immigration and conspiracy to facilitate breach of immigration law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States has a penalty of a $250,000 fine and five-year prison sentence for such arrangements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) and the Justice Department say that they do not have accurate numbers on the rate of attempted marriage fraud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In the 2009 fiscal year, 506 of the 241,154 petitions filed were denied for suspected fraud, a rate of 0.2%; seven percent were denied on other grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_and_political_status">Legal and political status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Legal and political status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">Illegal immigration to the United States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Illegal immigration in the United Kingdom">Illegal immigration in the United Kingdom</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_immigration" title="Australian immigration">Australian immigration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">Immigration to Canada</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_Pakistan" title="Illegal immigration to Pakistan">Illegal immigration to Pakistan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrants_in_Malaysia" title="Illegal immigrants in Malaysia">Illegal immigrants in Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Chile" title="Immigration to Chile">Immigration to Chile</a></i>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>Many countries have had or currently have laws restricting immigration for economic or <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalistic</a> political reasons or others. Whether a person is permitted to stay in a country legally may be decided by <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Quota_Act" title="Emergency Quota Act">quotas</a> or point systems or may be based on considerations such as family ties (marriage, elderly mother, etc.). Exceptions relative to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_refugee" title="Political refugee">political refugees</a> or to sick people are also common. In some countries, people born on national territory (henceforth not "immigrants") do not automatically obtain the nationality of their birthplace, and may have no legal title of residency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most countries have laws requiring workers to have proper documentation, often intended to prevent or minimize the employment of illegal immigrants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However the penalties against employers are often small and the acceptable identification requirements vague, ill-defined and seldom checked or enforced, making it easy for employers to hire illegal labor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Where the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> is several times the prevailing wage in the home country, employers sometimes pay less than the legal minimum wage or have unsafe working conditions, relying on the reluctance of illegal workers to report the violations to the authorities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In response to the outcry following popular knowledge of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, the newly established <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> held an international conference on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">refugees</a> to adopt the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" title="Convention relating to the Status of Refugees">Convention relating to the Status of Refugees</a> whereby refugees (legally defined to be people who are persecuted in their original country and then enter another country seeking safety) should be exempted from immigration laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> It is, however, up to the countries involved to decide if a particular immigrant is a refugee or not, and hence whether they are subject to the immigration controls.</p>
<p>Article 13 on the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a> declares the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">right to leave any country</a>, including one's own, to be a fundamental human right. The declaration does not state any right for an individual to <i>enter</i> a country other than his or her own. The same article also states a right to freely move within one's own country.</p>
<p>Illegal immigrants usually have no or very limited access to <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> systems, proper housing, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banks</a>. Some immigrants <a href="/wiki/Forgery" title="Forgery">forge</a> identity documents to get the access.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Amnesties waive the "subject to deportation" clause associated with illegal immigrants.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="By_country_or_region">By country or region</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: By country or region">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote plainlinks" role="note">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angola">Angola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Angola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Angola" title="Illegal immigration in Angola">Illegal immigration in Angola</a></div>
<p>In 2007 around 44,000 Congolese were forced to leave <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Since 2004, more than 400,000 illegal immigrants, almost all from the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, have been expelled from Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigration_in_Australia" title="Immigration in Australia">Immigration in Australia</a></div>
<p>Official government sources put the number of visa overstayers in Australia at approximately 50,000. This has been the official number of illegal immigrants for about 25 years and is considered to be low. Other sources have placed it at up to 100,000, but no detailed study has been completed to quantify this number, which could be significantly higher.</p>
<p>On 1 June 2013, the <i>Migration Amendment (Reform of Employer Sanctions) Act 2013</i> commenced. This new law puts the onus on businesses to ensure that their employees maintain the necessary work entitlements in Australia. The new legislation also enables the Australian Department of Immigration and Citizenship to levy infringement notices against business (AUD $15,300) and individual (AUD $3,060) employers on a <a href="/wiki/Strict_liability" title="Strict liability">strict liability</a> basis - meaning that there is no requirement to prove fault, negligence or intention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are about 1.2 million Indians living in Bangladesh illegally as of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The illegal migrants are mainly from the poorest states in India including <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manipur" title="Manipur">Manipur</a>, which surround Bangladesh. They illegally immigrate to Bangladesh in search of jobs in the metropolitan hubs and a better standard of living. Bangladesh is fifth among the nations sending highest <a href="/wiki/Remittances_to_India" title="Remittances to India">remittances to India</a>. Indians working in Bangladesh sent more than $3.7 billion back to India in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a significant number of Burmese illegal immigrants in Bangladesh. As of 2012, the Bangladesh government estimated about 500,000 illegal Burmese immigrants living across Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bhutan">Bhutan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bhutan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Bhutan" title="Illegal immigration in Bhutan">Illegal immigration in Bhutan</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigration_in_Bhutan" title="Immigration in Bhutan">Immigration in Bhutan</a> by Nepalese settlers (<a href="/wiki/Lhotshampa" title="Lhotshampa">Lhotshampa</a>) began slowly towards the end of the 19th century. The government passed the <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_Citizenship_Act_1985" title="Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1985">Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1985</a> to clarify and try to enforce the <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_Citizenship_Act_1958" title="Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1958">Bhutanese Citizenship Act 1958</a> to control the flood of illegal immigration. Those individuals who could not provide proof of residency prior to 1958 were adjudged to be illegal immigrants. In 1991 and 1992, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> expelled roughly 139,110 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepalis</a>, most of whom have been living in seven refugee camps in eastern Nepal ever since. The United States has offered to resettle 60,000 of the 107,000 <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_refugees" title="Bhutanese refugees">Bhutanese refugees</a> of Nepalese origin now living in U.N. refugee camps in Nepal. The Bhutanese government, even today, has not been able to sort the problem of giving citizenship to those people who are married to Bhutanese, even though they have been in the country for 40 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Brazil" title="Illegal immigration in Brazil">Illegal immigration in Brazil</a></div>
<p>Brazil has long been part of international migration routes. In 2009, the government estimated the number of illegal immigrants at about 200,000 people; a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> charity working with immigrants said there were 600,000 illegal immigrants (75,000 of which from <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>). That same year, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_Parliament" title="Brazilian Parliament">Brazilian Parliament</a> approved an amnesty, opening a six-month window for all foreigners to seek legalization irrespective of their previous standing before the law. Brazil had last legalized all immigrants in 1998; bilateral deals, one of which promoted the legalization of all reciprocal immigrants with Bolivia to date, signed in 2005, are also common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globo_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Globo-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Illegal immigrants in Brazil enjoy the same legal privileges as native Brazilians regarding access to social services such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">public education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_%C3%9Anico_de_Sa%C3%BAde" title="Sistema Único de Saúde">Brazilian public healthcare system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globo_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Globo-86">[86]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Police_Department" title="Federal Police Department">Federal Police</a> operation investigated Chinese immigrants who traveled through six countries before arriving in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> to work under substandard conditions in the <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textile industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>After signing the 2009 amnesty bill into law, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_Lula" title="President Lula">President Lula</a> said, in a speech, that "repression and intolerance against immigrants will not solve the problems caused by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_economic_crisis" title="2008 economic crisis">the economic crisis</a>", thereby also harshly criticizing the "policy of discrimination and prejudice" against immigrants in developed nations.</p>
<p>An October 2009 piece from <a href="/wiki/O_Globo" title="O Globo">O Globo</a>, quoting a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNDP" title="UNDP">UNDP</a> study, estimates the number of illegal immigrants at 0.7 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> and points out to a recent wave of xenophobia among the general populace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Canada" title="Illegal immigration in Canada">Illegal immigration in Canada</a></div>
<p>There is no credible information available on illegal immigration in Canada. Estimates range between 35,000 and 120,000 illegal immigrants in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Byron_Bissett" title="James Byron Bissett">James Bissett</a>, a former head of the Canadian Immigration Service, has suggested that the lack of any credible refugee screening process, combined with a high likelihood of ignoring any deportation orders, has resulted in tens of thousands of outstanding warrants for the arrest of rejected refugee claimants, with little attempt at enforcement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Refugee claimants in Canada do not have to attempt re-entry to learn the status of their claim. A 2008 report by the <a href="/wiki/Auditor_General_of_Canada" title="Auditor General of Canada">Auditor General</a> <a href="/wiki/Sheila_Fraser" title="Sheila Fraser">Sheila Fraser</a> stated that Canada has lost track of as many as 41,000 illegal immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> This number was predicted to increase drastically with the expiration of <a href="/wiki/Temporary_foreign_worker_program_in_Canada" title="Temporary foreign worker program in Canada">temporary employer work permits</a> issued in 2007 and 2008, which were not renewed in many cases because of the shortage of work due to the recession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> has recently become a new pole of attraction for illegal immigrants, mostly from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> but also <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>. According to the 2002 national census, Chile's foreign-born foreign population has increased by 75% since 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_China" title="Illegal immigration in China">Illegal immigration in China</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> is building a security barrier along its border with <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> to prevent the <a href="/wiki/North_Korean_defectors" title="North Korean defectors">defectors or refugees from North Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Also, many immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> have tried to make it to China. There might be as many as 100,000 Africans in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, mostly illegal overstayers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> To encourage people to report foreigners living illegally in China, the police is giving a 100 yuan reward to whistleblowers whose information successfully leads to an expulsion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Haitians_in_the_Dominican_Republic" title="Haitians in the Dominican Republic">Haitians in the Dominican Republic</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> is a nation that shares the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> with <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>. An estimated 1,000,000 Haitians live and work in the Dominican Republic. The percentage of Haitians that have illegally immigrated to the Dominican Republic is not accurately known, and "many Dominicans have come to resent the influx of lower-paid workers from across the border and have sought to make their country less hospitable to noncitizens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_India" title="Illegal immigration in India">Illegal immigration in India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bangladeshi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bangladeshi.jpg/220px-Bangladeshi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bangladeshi.jpg/330px-Bangladeshi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Bangladeshi.jpg/440px-Bangladeshi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bangladeshi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
ABVP against Bangladeshi illegal immigrants</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It is estimated that several tens of millions of illegal immigrants live in India. Precise figures are not available, but the numbers run in tens of millions, at least 10 million are from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, others being from <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">Bangladesh Liberation War</a> at least 10 million Bangladeshis crossed into India illegally to seek refuge from widespread <a href="/wiki/Rape_during_the_Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Rape during the Bangladesh Liberation War">rape</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1971_Bangladesh_Genocide" title="1971 Bangladesh Genocide">genocide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes-101">[101]</a></sup> According to Indian Home Ministry, at least 1.4 Million Bangladeshi crossed over into India in the last decade alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes-101">[101]</a></sup> Samir Guha Roy of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Statistical_Institute" title="Indian Statistical Institute">Indian Statistical Institute</a> called these estimates "motivatedly exaggerated". After examining the population growth and demographic statistics, Roy instead states that a significant numbers of internal migration is sometimes falsely thought to be immigrants. An analysis of the numbers by Roy revealed that on average around 91000 Bangladeshi nationals might have crossed over to India every year during the years 1981-1991 but how many of them where identified and pushed back is not known. It is possible that a large portion of these immigrants returned on their own to their place of origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facingglobal_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-facingglobal-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to a pro-Indian scholar, the trip to India from Bangladesh is one of the cheapest in the world, with a trip costing around Rs.2000 (around $30 US), which includes the fee for the "Tour Operator". As Bangladeshis are cultural similar to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengali_people" title="Bengali people">Bengali people</a> in India, they are able to pass off as Indian citizens and settle down in any part of India to establish a future.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes-101">[101]</a></sup> for a very small price. This false identity can be bolstered with false documentation available for as little as Rs.200 ($3 US) can even make them part of the vote bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facingglobal_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-facingglobal-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the Bengali speaking people deported from Maharashtra as illegal immigrants are originally Indian citizens from West Bengal. Police would demand 2000-2500 from each of the detained Bengali speaking people for their release. If they fail to pay that amount, they are kept behind the bar for 10–15 days following which they would be taken to border and pushed into Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facingglobal_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-facingglobal-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>India is constructing barriers on its eastern borders to combat the surge of migrants. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Bangladeshi_barrier" title="Indo-Bangladeshi barrier">Indo-Bangladeshi barrier</a> is 4,000 km (2,500 mi) long. Presently, India is constructing a fence along the border to restrict illegal traffic from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> This obstruction will virtually isolate Bangladesh from India. The barrier's plan is based on the designs of the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">Israeli West Bank barrier</a> and will be 3.6 m (11.8 ft) high. The stated aim of the fence is to stop infiltration of terrorists, prevent smuggling, and end illegal immigration from Bangladesh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/46_illegal_Afghan_immigrants_suffocate_in_truck_in_Pakistan" title="wikinews:46 illegal Afghan immigrants suffocate in truck in Pakistan">46 illegal Afghan immigrants suffocate in truck in Pakistan</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Since late April 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> government has forcibly deported back to <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> mostly unregistered (and some registered) <a href="/wiki/Afghans_in_Iran" title="Afghans in Iran">Afghans living and working in Iran</a> at a rate between 250,000 and 300,000 per year. The forceful evictions of the refugees, who lived in Iran and Pakistan for nearly three decades, are part of the two countries' larger plans to repatriate all Afghan refugees within a few years. Iran says that it will send 1,000,000 by next March, and Pakistan announced that all 2,400,000 Afghan refugees, most living in camps, must return home by 2009. Experts<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2010)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> say it will be "disastrous" for Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_from_Africa_to_Israel" title="Illegal immigration from Africa to Israel">Illegal immigration from Africa to Israel</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:There_Are_No_Illegal_Children!.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg/220px-There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg/330px-There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg/440px-There_Are_No_Illegal_Children%21.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:There_Are_No_Illegal_Children!.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Demonstration against the expulsion of illegal immigrants and their families from Israel, Tel Aviv, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tens of thousands of migrants, mostly from Sudan and Eritrea, had crossed the Israeli border between 2009 and 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a> said that "This phenomenon is very grave and threatens the social fabric of society, our national security and our national identity."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In May 2012, Israel introduced a law which would allow illegal immigrants to be detained for up to three years, a measure that the Interior Ministry intended to stem the flow of Africans entering Israel across the desert border with Egypt.</p>
