<p>Israel faces substantial illegal immigration of Arab workers from the Palestinian Authority territories, a migration that includes both workers seeking employment, and homosexuals escaping the social approbation of Arab society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Shipwreck_off_coast_of_Libya;_hundreds_of_African_migrants_feared_dead" title="wikinews:Shipwreck off coast of Libya; hundreds of African migrants feared dead">Shipwreck off coast of Libya; hundreds of African migrants feared dead</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Libya" title="Illegal immigration in Libya">Illegal immigration in Libya</a></div>
<p>Before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libyan_civil_war" title="Libyan civil war">Libyan civil war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> was home to a large illegal <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan African</a> population which numbers as much as 2,000,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The mass expulsion plan to summarily deport all illegal foreigners was announced by then-current Libyan leader Colonel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muammar_al-Gaddafi" title="Muammar al-Gaddafi">Muammar al-Gaddafi</a> in January 2008, "No resident without a legal visa will be excluded."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia">Malaysia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Malaysia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_Malaysia" title="Illegal immigration to Malaysia">Illegal immigration to Malaysia</a></div>
<p>There are an estimated 800,000 illegal immigrants in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In January 2009, Malaysia banned the hiring of foreign workers in factories, stores and restaurants to protect its citizens from mass unemployment amid the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_2000s_recession" title="Late 2000s recession">late 2000s recession</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> An ethnic <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_Indian" title="Malaysian Indian">Indian Malaysian</a> was recently sentenced to whipping and 10 months in prison for hiring six illegal immigrants at his restaurant. "I think that after this, Malaysian employers will be afraid to take in foreign workers (without work permits). They will think twice", said immigration department prosecutor Azlan Abdul Latiff. "This is the first case where an employer is being sentenced to caning", he said. illegal immigrants also face <a href="/wiki/Caning" title="Caning">caning</a> before being deported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Mexico" title="Illegal immigration in Mexico">Illegal immigration in Mexico</a></div>
<p>In the first six months of 2005, more than 120,000 people from <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> were deported, as compared to 2002, when for the entire year, only 130,000 were deported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> People of <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> origin pay about $5,500 to smugglers to be taken to Mexico from <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>. It is estimated that 2.4% of rejections for work permits in Mexico correspond to Chinese citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In a 2010 news story, <i>USA Today</i> reported, "... Mexico's <a href="/wiki/Arizona_SB_1070" title="Arizona SB 1070">Arizona-style</a> law requires local police to check IDs. And Mexican police freely engage in <a href="/wiki/Racial_profiling" title="Racial profiling">racial profiling</a> and routinely harass Central American migrants, say immigration activists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many women from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, Asia, and <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central</a> and South America take jobs at <a href="/wiki/Table_dance" title="Table dance">table dance</a> establishments in large cities. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Migration" title="National Institute of Migration">National Institute of Migration</a> (INM) in Mexico raids <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strip_clubs" title="Strip clubs">strip clubs</a> and deports foreigners who work without proper documentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2004, the INM deported 188,000 people at a cost of US$10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2007, Mexican President Calderón harshly criticized the United States government for the crackdown on illegal immigrants, saying it has led to the persecution of immigrant workers without visas. "I have said that Mexico does not stop at its border, that wherever there is a Mexican, there is Mexico", he said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> However, Mexico has also deported US citizens, deporting 2,000 cases in 2015 and 1,243 in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Illegal immigration of Cubans through <a href="/wiki/Canc%C3%BAn" title="Cancún">Cancún</a> tripled from 2004 to 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In October 2008, Mexico tightened its immigration rules and agreed to deport <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">Cubans</a> who use the country as an entry point to the US. It also criticized US policy that generally allows Cubans who reach US territory to stay. Cuban Foreign Minister said the Cuban-Mexican agreement would lead to "the immense majority of Cubans being repatriated."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Maoist)" title="Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)">Maoist</a>-led government has initiated a major crackdown against Tibetan exiles with the aim to deport to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetans" title="Tibetans">Tibetans</a> living illegally in the country. Tibetans started pouring in Nepal after a failed anti-Chinese <a href="/wiki/1959_Tibetan_uprising" title="1959 Tibetan uprising">uprising in Tibet</a> in 1959.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Pakistan#Illegal_aliens" title="Immigration to Pakistan">Immigration to Pakistan § Illegal aliens</a></div>
<p>As of 2005, 2.1% of the population of <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> had foreign origins, however the number of immigrants population in Pakistan recently grew sharply. Immigrants from <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> make up a growing proportion of immigrants in Pakistan. The five largest immigrant groups in Pakistan are in turn <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghans</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladeshi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tajik_people" title="Tajik people">Tajiks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkmen_people" title="Turkmen people">Turkmens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Iranians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_India" title="Islam in India">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Moors" title="Sri Lankan Moors">Sri Lankan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rohingya_people" title="Rohingya people">Burmese</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britons</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> including a sizeable number of those of Pakistani origin. Other significant <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> communities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australians" title="Australians">Australians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Americans</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moro_people" title="Moro people">Filipinos</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosnians</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and many others. Migrants from different countries of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_World" title="Arab World">Arab world</a> specially <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> are in thousands. Nearly all illegal migrants in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> refugees and they are accepted by the local population. There is no political support or legislation to deport these refugees from <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It was estimated by Teresita Ang-See, a prominent leader and activist of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Filipino" title="Chinese Filipino">Chinese Filipino</a> community, that by 2007, as much as 100,000 illegal immigrants from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> are living in the Philippines, a tenth of the ethnic Chinese population. The latest influx has come in part because of Manila's move in 2005 to liberalise entry procedures for Chinese tourists and investors, a move that helped triple the number of Chinese visitors to 133,000 last year. Many of the new Chinese immigrants encounter hostility from many Filipinos, including Filipino-born Chinese, for being perceived as engaging in criminal activities and fraud.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Russia" title="Illegal immigration in Russia">Illegal immigration in Russia</a></div>
<p>Russia experiences a constant flow of immigration. On average, 200,000 legal immigrants enter the country every year; about half are ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> from other republics of the former Soviet Union. In addition, there are an estimated 10–12 million unauthorized immigrants in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> There has been a significant influx of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T%C4%81jik_people" title="Tājik people">Tajiks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> into large Russian cities in recent years, which has been viewed very unfavorably by many citizens and contributed to <a href="/wiki/Russian_nationalism" title="Russian nationalism">nationalist</a> sentiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many immigrant ethnic groups have much higher birth rates than native Russians, further shifting the balance. Some <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> flee the overpopulation and birth control regulations of their home country and settle in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Far East</a> and in southern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. Russia's main Pacific port and naval base of <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>, once closed to foreigners, today is bristling with Chinese markets, restaurants and trade houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> This has been occurring a lot since the Soviet collapse.</p>
<p>Illegal border crossing is considered a crime, and captured illegal border crossers have been sentenced to prison terms. For example, <i><a href="/wiki/Rossiyskaya_Gazeta" title="Rossiyskaya Gazeta">Rossiyskaya Gazeta</a></i> reported in October 2008 the case of a <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korean</a> who was detained after illegally crossing the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" title="Amur River">Amur River</a> from China. Considered by Russian authorities an "<a href="/wiki/Economic_migrant" title="Economic migrant">economic migrant</a>", he was sentenced to 6 months in prison and was to be deported to the country of his nationality after serving his sentence, even though he may now risk an even heavier penalty there. That was just one of the 26 cases year-to-date of illegal entrants, of various nationalities, receiving criminal punishment in <a href="/wiki/Amur_Oblast" title="Amur Oblast">Amur Oblast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Saudi_Arabia" title="Illegal immigration in Saudi Arabia">Illegal immigration in Saudi Arabia</a></div>
<p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> began construction of a <a href="/wiki/Saudi%E2%80%93Yemen_barrier" title="Saudi–Yemen barrier">Saudi–Yemen barrier</a> between its territory and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> to prevent the unauthorized movement of people and goods into and out of the Kingdom. Anthony H. Cordesman labeled it a "separation barrier."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In February 2004, <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a> reported that Yemeni opposition newspapers likened the barrier to the Israeli West Bank barrier,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gdn1_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gdn1-148">[148]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a> wrote "Saudi Arabia, one of the most vocal critics in the Arab world of Israel's 'security fence' in the West Bank, is quietly emulating the Israeli example by erecting a barrier along its porous border with Yemen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Saudi officials rejected the comparison saying it was built to prevent infiltration and smuggling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gdn1_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gdn1-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schengen_Area">Schengen Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Schengen Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">European migrant crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/220px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/330px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/440px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants along the Balkan route crossing from Serbia into Hungary, 24 August 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Schengen Area is a multilateral agreement between 26 states in which they in most cases abolish the border control between themselves. These states include most of the EU countries, as well as the EEC countries Norway, Switzerland and Iceland. Any person who is physically inside any of the Schengen states will usually be able to travel to any other Schengen state without hindrance from the law enforcement, even if he or she has no legal right to enter another Schengen Area member state. A person who wishes to immigrate illegally to a Schengen Area member state may therefore find it more practical to enter it through another member state. According to a BBC report from 2012, over 80% of illegal immigrants entering the European Union pass through Greece.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>EU countries that are not members of the Schengen Agreement are still committed to allow lawful entry by citizens of EU countries;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> they may however exercise border control at their discretion. This typically presents a significant hindrance to persons who are trying to enter those countries illegally. The Schengen Agreement does not regulate treatment of persons who enter the Schengen Area illegally. This is therefore left to the individual states, and other applicable international treaties and European <a href="/wiki/Case_law" title="Case law">case law</a>. Illegal immigration to Schengen and to Europe in general was increasing sharply since approximately early 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The main causes for this increase are the conflicts that followed the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>; in particular, the civil war in Syria has driven millions of people from their homes, and the disintegration of the Libyan government removed a major barrier for the African migrants.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1382" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:East_German_Guard_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
East German border guard Conrad Schumman jumping the border in 1961</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Illegal immigration to some of the Schengen Area states might face different consideration depending on countries such as Bulgaria, France, Greece.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2013, 11000 people attempted to go into <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> via its border with Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_04August2015_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent_04August2015-153">[153]</a></sup> Their aim is not believed by Bulgarian border officials to remain in Bulgaria, but to go to other European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_04August2015_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent_04August2015-153">[153]</a></sup> In November 2013 Bulgaria started building a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Razor_wire" title="Razor wire">razor wire</a> fence on its Turkey border which was completed in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_04August2015_153-2"><a href="#cite_note-independent_04August2015-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_France" title="Immigration to France">Immigration to France</a></div>
<p>Children born to noncitizens in France are not immigrants themselves, but they are considered foreigners under French law, until they reach the age of 18, at which time they automatically become citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-migrationinformation.org_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-migrationinformation.org-154">[154]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_citizenship" title="French citizenship">French citizenship</a> is based in the idea of political unity; therefore, French citizenship may be more accessible than other EU countries, such as Germany and the UK. However, many French citizens feel that those who gain French citizenship should conform to the cultural aspects of French life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Foreigners can also become French citizens if they serve in the <a href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Legion" title="French Foreign Legion">Foreign Legion</a>.</p>
<p>French law prohibits anyone from assisting or trying to assist "the entry, movement, or irregular stay of a foreigner in France." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-156">[156]</a></sup> France has an Immigration Ministry (L'immigration, l'intégration, l'asile et le développement solidaire) which begun functioning in 2007 under President Sarkozy. The government seek to combat smugglers who profit financially from moving immigrants into, through, and out of France, according to the Immigration Minister, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Besson" title="Éric Besson">Éric Besson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-migrationinformation.org_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-migrationinformation.org-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc.msn.com_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc.msn.com-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Greece" title="Immigration to Greece">Immigration to Greece</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_border_barrier" title="Hungarian border barrier">Hungarian border barrier</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1280" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg/220px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg/330px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg/440px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Serbia_border_fence" title="Hungary–Serbia border fence">Hungarian–Serbian border fence</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2014, Hungary registered 43000 asylum seekers and 80000 up to July 2015.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the summer of 2015 <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> started building <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_southern_border_fence" title="Hungarian southern border fence">a 4m high fence</a> along its 175 km border to neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to keep out the tens of thousands illegal immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and migrants trying to reach the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smh_17jul2015_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-smh_17jul2015-157">[157]</a></sup> The border was sealed on 15 September 2015 and the fence was the following day attacked by refugees and defended by riot police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gam_16sep2015_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-gam_16sep2015-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the Hungary-Serbia border closed, migrants then started heading to Croatia, but as Croatia led the migrants to the Hungary-Croatia border, Hungary then started the construction of a second fence along its border with Croatia on 18 September 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dw_18.09.2015_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-dw_18.09.2015-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Italy" title="Immigration to Italy">Immigration to Italy</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_South_Africa" title="Illegal immigration in South Africa">Illegal immigration in South Africa</a></div>
<p>No accurate estimates of the number of undocumented migrants living in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chiumia_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chiumia-160">[160]</a></sup> Estimates that have been published vary widely. A 1996 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Sciences_Research_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Human Sciences Research Council (page does not exist)">Human Sciences Research Council</a> study estimated that there were between 2.5 million and 4.1 million undocumented migrants in the country. In their 2008/09 annual report, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Police_Service" title="South African Police Service">South African Police Service</a> stated: "According to various estimates, the number of undocumented immigrants in South Africa may vary between three and six million people". Other estimates have put the figure as high as 10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-161">[161]</a></sup> As of April 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Statistics_South_Africa" title="Statistics South Africa">Statistics South Africa</a>'s official estimate is of between 500,000 and one million undocumented migrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mwiti_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mwiti-162">[162]</a></sup> A large number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zimbabweans" title="Zimbabweans">Zimbabweans</a> have fled to South Africa as a result of instability in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, with many living as undocumented migrants in South Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chiumia_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chiumia-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRIN_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-IRIN-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloch_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloch-163">[163]</a></sup> Sociologist Alice Bloch notes that migrants in South Africa have been the victims of <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia_in_South_Africa" title="Xenophobia in South Africa">xenophobia</a> and violence, regardless of their immigration status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloch_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bloch-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the Republic of Korea Immigration Service, as of 31 December 2012, there were 177,854 illegal immigrants, which is 12.3% of 1,445,103 total foreign nationals who resided in South Korea. The top 10 home countries of those illegal immigrants were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Philippines" title="The Philippines">The Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_United_States_of_America" title="The United States of America">The United States of America</a>, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the US-led invasion of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> in March 2003, there are more <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_Iraq" title="Refugees of Iraq">refugees from Iraq</a> . The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimates that nearly 2,200,000 <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqis</a> have fled the country since 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> with nearly 100,000 fleeing to <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> each month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Most ventured to Jordan and Syria, creating demographic shifts that have worried both governments. Refugees are mired in poverty as they are generally barred from working in their host countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>Syrian authorities worried that the new influx of refugees would limit the country's resources. Sources like oil, heat, water and electricity were said to be becoming scarcer as demand were rising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> On 1 October 2007, news agencies reported that Syria reimposed restrictions on Iraqi refugees, as stated by a spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>. Under Syria's new rules, only Iraqi merchants, businessmen and university professors with visas acquired from Syrian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embassy" title="Embassy">embassies</a> may enter Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_Turkey" title="Illegal immigration in Turkey">Illegal immigration in Turkey</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> receives many economic migrants from nearby countries such as <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, but also from <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> is thought to have increased the flow of illegal immigration into Turkey, and the global parties directly involved in the conflict have been accused of extending a less-helping hand than Turkey itself to resolve the precarious situation of immigrants stranded in passage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Illegal immigration in the United Kingdom">Illegal immigration in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>Many try to cross the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> from <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> to seek asylum or refugee status in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-177">[177]</a></sup> Truck drivers can be fined up to €2,500 if illegal immigrants are found on board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The Home Office has it's agents working alongside French police and immigration agents, to prevent unauthorized people from entering the zone. An area of Calais known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calais_jungle" title="Calais jungle">"the Jungle"</a> had a police raid in September 2009 to control illegal immigration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-time.com-177">[177]</a></sup> The French also try to stop illegals from entering France from the southern part of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Non-governmental organizations, such as Secours Catholique and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> provide food, showers, and shelter to sans papiers who gather waiting to cross the Channel.</p>
<p>In 1986, an Iranian man was sent back to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, as he was unable to present any ID to British immigration officers. He stayed at the airport for nearly twenty years and his story was made into a film, <a href="/wiki/The_Terminal" title="The Terminal">The Terminal</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were between 550,000 and 950,000 illegal immigrants in the United Kingdom. The United Kingdom is a difficult country to reach as it is mostly located on one island and part of another, but traffickers in <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> have tried to smuggle illegal immigrants into the UK. Many illegal immigrants come from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. As of 2008 there were also many from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> having overstayed their visas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2012 study carried out by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>'s Centre on Migration, Policy and Society (COMPAS) has estimated that there were 120,000 irregular migrant children in the UK, of whom 65,000 were born in the UK to parents without legal status. According to the study these children are at risk of destitution, exploitation and social exclusion because of contradictory and frequently changing rules and regulations which jeopardize their access to healthcare, education, protection by the police and other public services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> estimated that 4,000 to 10,000 applications a year to stay in the UK are made on the basis of a <a href="/wiki/Sham_marriage" title="Sham marriage">sham marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Many illegal immigrants or asylum seekers have tried to enter the UK from France, by hiding inside trucks or trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">Illegal immigration to the United States</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg/170px-May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg/255px-May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg/340px-May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:May_Day_Immigration_March_LA47.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Illegal immigrant rights march for amnesty in downtown Los Angeles, California on <a href="/wiki/International_Workers%27_Day" title="International Workers' Day">May Day</a>, 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Approximately 11 million illegal immigrants are estimated to be living in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Estimates from the Pew Hispanic Center show the number of illegal immigrants has declined to 11.1 million in March 2009 from a peak of 12 million in March 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The majority of the illegal immigrants are from Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Illegal immigration has long been controversial.</p>
<p>In 2007, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> called for Congress to endorse his guest worker proposal, stating that illegal immigrants took jobs that Americans would not take.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-189">[189]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pew_Hispanic_Center" title="Pew Hispanic Center">Pew Hispanic Center</a> notes that while the number of legal immigrants arriving has not varied substantially since the 1980s, the number of illegal immigrants has increased dramatically and, since the mid-1990s, has surpassed the number of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">legal immigrants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Penalties for employers of illegal immigrants, of $2,000–$10,000 and up to six months' imprisonment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> go largely unenforced.</p>
<p>Political groups like Americans for Legal Immigration<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> have been formed to demand enforcement of immigration laws and secure borders. ALIPAC has also called for "safe departure" border checkpoints, free of criminal checks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2011 news story, <i>Los Angeles Times</i> reported,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>... illegal immigrants in 2010 were parents of 5.5 million children, 4.5 million of whom were <a href="/wiki/Anchor_baby" title="Anchor baby">born in the U.S.</a> and are citizens. Because illegal immigrants are younger and more likely to be married, they represented a disproportionate share of births—8% of the babies born in the U.S. between March 2009 and March 2010 were to at least one illegal immigrant parent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Immigration from Mexico to the United States has slowed in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> This has been attributed to the slowing of the U.S. economy, the buildup in security along the border and increased violence on the Mexican side of the border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico#Illegal_immigration" title="Dominican immigration to Puerto Rico">Dominican immigration to Puerto Rico#Illegal immigration</a></i></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Illegal_immigration&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An estimated 200,000 Colombians have fled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_civil_war_(1964%E2%80%93present)" title="Colombian civil war (1964–present)">Colombian civil war</a> and sought safety in Venezuela. Most of them lack identity documents and this hampers their access to services, as well as to the labor market. The Venezuelan government has no specific policies on refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Maritime operations</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
